## <a name='project-details'>1. Project Details</a>

A simple machine learning pipeline built based on mashable dataset. The objective is to predict the number of s hares (popularity) on social media platforms for the
news articles.

## <a name='overview'>2. Overview of submitted folder and the folder structure</a>

An overview of the submitted folder and structure is as below:


```flow
|--src
|   |-- preprocessing.py
|   |-- ml_model.py
|--data
|   |-- news_popularity.db (Not included in submission)
|-- README.md
|-- eda.ipynb
|-- requirements.txt
|-- run.sh
```

<b>src folder</b>


The preprocessing.py module contains the feature_preprocessing function that extracts data and perform data preparation before feeding into the ML model.
It includes one-hot encoding categorical variables, scaling the data and splitting the dataset.


The ML model contains the 4 models used for this simple machine learning pipeline: (1) ElasticNet, (2) Gradient Boosting, (3) Support Vector Machines (Ensemble-Bagging) and (4) Logistic Regression (Ensemble-Bagging)
Other legacy models that were experimented on were left commented out and may be re-activated on a later date if necessary.


<b>data</b>

Contains the database file to be accessed. (Left empty in submission as instructed)


<b>README.md</b>

This is the file that contains information on the Simple Machine Learning Pipeline


<b>eda.ipynb</b>

Jupyter Notebook on the exploratory data analysis with visualisations.


<b>requirements.txt</b>

Run 'pip install -r requirements.txt' to install the necessary packages to run this Simple Machine learning Pipeline
 

<b>run.sh</b>

An executable shell script to run the ML models

## <a name='instruction'>3. Instructions for executing the pipeline and modifying any parameters</a>

Please refer below for the instructions of executing the pipeline:
1. Type './run.sh' in the Ubuntu terminal
2. Key in the approach, 'Regression' or 'Classification'
3. If 'Regression' is selected, the options 'GradientBoosting' or 'ElasticNet' will appear. Input either of them.
   If 'Classification' is selected, the options 'SupportVector_Bagging' or 'LogisticRegression_Bagging' will appear. Input either of them.
4. It will then ask if you would like running with the default feature list or your own features. Input 'ok' to use the default feature list. Otherwise, input the features you want separated by spaces. (e.g. 'timedelta n_comments num_keywords kw_avg_avg')
5. This will generate an output of Mean Squared Error(MSE), Root Mean Squared Error(RMSE), Mean Absolute Error(MAE), model selected and features selected after it has completed running

FFABRRRQAUUUUAFFFFABRRRQAUUUUAFFFFABRRRQB//Z'>


## <a name='step-flow'>4. Description of logical steps/flow of the pipeline</a>

The pipeline comprises of data ingestion, data storage, data processing, ML model and data consumption (output)


Data ingestion: The data is taken from Mashable website

Data storage: The data is stored in SQL after ETL (e.g. timedelta, n_comments, num_keywords, etc.)

Data processing: The data stored in db format is preprocessed by the function in preprocessing.py

ML model: The ML models are in ml_model.py and can be accessed using run.sh

Data consumption (Output): The evaluation metrics are produced after run.sh completes running

## <a name='key-finding'>5. Key findings from the EDA conducted</a>

After performing exploratory data analysis, the following were observed:
1. The dataset is obtained from Mashable, an American entertainment, culture, tech, science and social good digital media platform, news website and multi-platform media and entertainment company.
2. The date range of data collection is from 2013/01/07 to 2014/12/27
3. Average number of shares: 2913.7284057010274
4. Maximum number of shares: 663600
5. Minimum number of shares: 5
6. Dropping empty fields reduced the dataset from 39,644 to 15,085
7. Columns such as url, weekdays, data_channel will need to undergo feature engineering (e.g. monday to 1, tuesday to 2, etc.)
8. The standard deviation for some of the values are relatively high and will need to undergo normalisation (i.e. scaling) so that the distribution do not have outrageous outliers.
9. Variables will be check for correlation with shares
10. Feature-cross can be explored

From the visualisations and correlations observed, the proposed features are as follows:
1. timedelta
2. num_hrefs
3. n_comments
4. self_reference_min_shares (optional with self_reference_avg_shares)
5. self_reference_max_shares (optional with self_reference_avg_shares)
6. self_reference_avg_shares
7. num_keywords
8. kw_max_min (optional with kw_avg_min)
9. kw_avg_min
10. kw_max_avg (optional with kw_avg_avg)
11. kw_avg_avg
12. weekday (to be one-hot)
13. n_tokens_title
14. data_channel (to be one-hot)
15. n_tokens_content (optional)

Too many features may cause overfitting so the above features (non-optional) are selected to be used in the ML models

## <a name='model-choice'>6. Explanation of choice of models for each machine learning task</a>

After taking into consideration the findings from the exploratory data analysis, the following models were selected for each respective task:

<u>Regression</u>
1. Gradient Boosting

    Gradient boosting produces a prediction model in the form of an ensemble of weak prediction models. This model is used to address the imbalanced data and will create a more generalised model for prediction.

2. ElasticNet

    Elastic Net is a combination of Ridge (that penalises sum of squared coefficients, L2) and Lasso (That penalises sum of absolute coefficients, L1). ElasticNet is used to create a more generalised model for prediction.


<u>Classification</u>

Bagging, an ensemble method is used to improve the predictions of both the base models.
    
1. Support Vector Machines - Bagging
    
    Support vector machines are effective in high dimensional spaces and is still effective when the number of dimensions is greater than the number of samples.

2. Logistic Regression - Bagging

    As some of the variables are categorical, Logistic Regression is explored to see if it provides any improvement over the other models.

A simple multi-level perceptron neural network was experimented but found to be lacking, due to the large number of classes vs data points.

## <a name='model-evaluation'>7. Evaluation of models developed</a>

The models were evaluated based on Mean Absolute Error (MAE). As the dataset was imbalanced, there were insufficient number in the respective classes in classification and extreme outliers were detrimental to regression methods.

The features used were identified during EDA. MAE is used as it is a more representative measure of the deviance from the actual number of shares.

GradientBoosting MAE: 1680.24

ElasticNet MAE: 2852.62

Support Vector Machines - Bagging MAE: 1587.93

Logistic Regression = Bagging: 1663.39

The ensemble methods were observed to perform better than normal ML methods (i.e. ElasticNet). In addition, the classification model performed better than the regression model. This is likely because binning shares into respective classes improved the prediction. However, the MAE of the classification model is unlikely to reach less than 1,000 as the shares were binned by thousands.

## <a name='other-considerations'>Other considerations for deploying the models developed</a>

Other considerations for deploying the model

1. Run 'pip3 install -r requirements.txt'
2. Put the database in the data folder
